<td style="width:50%;padding-left:0.25em">80,000</td>

</tr>
<tr>
<td style="width:50%;border-right:1px dotted #aaa;">~ 30,000 military killed<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hussenet_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-hussenet-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></td>
<td style="width:50%;padding-left:0.25em">~ 130,000 military and civilians killed<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hussenet_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-hussenet-1">[1]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="font-size:90%;border-top:1px solid #aaa;">Inhabitants of the Vendee: ~ 170,000 military and civilians killed (75 – 80% ; royalists and 20 – 25% republicans)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hussenet_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-hussenet-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><br/>
<br/>
170,000 – 200,000 dead in total<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></td>

<tr>
<td style="padding:0.3em 0.4em 0.3em;font-weight:bold;border-top: 1px solid #aaa; border-bottom: 1px solid #aaa;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:046CupolaSPietro.jpg"><img alt="046CupolaSPietro.jpg" class="noviewer" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/046CupolaSPietro.jpg/16px-046CupolaSPietro.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/046CupolaSPietro.jpg/24px-046CupolaSPietro.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/046CupolaSPietro.jpg/32px-046CupolaSPietro.jpg 2x" width="16"/></a> <a href="/wiki/Portal:Catholicism" title="Portal:Catholicism">Catholicism portal</a></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;">
<div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">
<ul>
<li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Persecutions_of_the_Catholic_Church_sidebar" title="Template:Persecutions of the Catholic Church sidebar"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Persecutions_of_the_Catholic_Church_sidebar" title="Template talk:Persecutions of the Catholic Church sidebar"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Persecutions_of_the_Catholic_Church_sidebar&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li>
</ul>
</div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The <b>War in the Vendée</b> (1793 to 1796; French: <span lang="fr" xml:lang="fr"><i>Guerre de Vendée</i></span>) was an uprising in the <a href="/wiki/Vend%C3%A9e" title="Vendée">Vendée</a> region of <a href="/wiki/French_First_Republic" title="French First Republic">France</a> during the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a>. The Vendée is a coastal region, located immediately south of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Loire_River" title="Loire River">Loire River</a> in western France. Initially, the war was similar to the 14th-century <a href="/wiki/Jacquerie" title="Jacquerie">Jacquerie</a> peasant uprising, but quickly acquired themes considered by the government in Paris to be <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Counter-revolution" title="Counter-revolution">counter-revolutionary</a>, and <a href="/wiki/House_of_Bourbon" title="House of Bourbon">Royalist</a>. The uprising headed by the self-styled <a href="/wiki/Catholic_and_Royal_Army" title="Catholic and Royal Army">Catholic and Royal Army</a> was comparable to the <a href="/wiki/Chouannerie" title="Chouannerie">Chouannerie</a>, which took place in the area north of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Loire_River" title="Loire River">Loire</a>.</p>
<p>The departments included in the uprising, called the <i>Vendée Militaire</i>, included the area between the Loire and the <a href="/wiki/Layon" title="Layon">Layon</a> rivers: Vendée (<a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Marais_(Vend%C3%A9e)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Marais (Vendée) (page does not exist)">Marais</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Bocage_Vend%C3%A9en&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Bocage Vendéen (page does not exist)">Bocage Vendéen</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Collines_Vend%C3%A9ennes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Collines Vendéennes (page does not exist)">Collines Vendéennes</a>), part of <a href="/wiki/Maine-et-Loire" title="Maine-et-Loire">Maine-et-Loire</a> west of the <a href="/wiki/Layon" title="Layon">Layon</a>, and the portion of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deux_S%C3%A8vres" title="Deux Sèvres">Deux Sèvres</a> west of the <a href="/wiki/Thouet" title="Thouet">River Thouet</a>. Having secured their <i>pays</i>, the deficiencies of the Vendean army became more apparent. Lacking a unified strategy (or army) and fighting a defensive campaign, from April onwards the army lost cohesion and its special advantages. Successes continued for some time: <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Thouars" title="Battle of Thouars">Thouars</a> was taken in early May and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Saumur_(1793)" title="Battle of Saumur (1793)">Saumur</a> in June; there were victories at <a href="/wiki/Maul%C3%A9on,_Deux-S%C3%A8vres" title="Mauléon, Deux-Sèvres">Châtillon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vihiers" title="Vihiers">Vihiers</a>. After this string of victories, the Vendeans turned to a protracted siege of <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Nantes" title="Battle of Nantes">Nantes</a>, for which they were unprepared and which stalled their momentum, giving the government in Paris sufficient time to send more troops and experienced generals.</p>
<p>Tens of thousands of civilians, Republican prisoners, and sympathizers with the revolution were massacred by both armies. Historians such as <a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reynald_Secher" title="fr:Reynald Secher">Reynald Secher</a> have described these events as '<a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a>,' but most scholars reject the use of the word as inaccurate. Ultimately, the uprising was suppressed using draconian measures. The historian <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Furet" title="François Furet">François Furet</a> concludes that the repression in the Vendée "not only revealed massacre and destruction on an unprecedented scale but also a zeal so violent that it has bestowed as its legacy much of the region's identity ... The war aptly epitomizes the depth of the conflict ... between religious tradition and the revolutionary foundation of democracy."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_the_Vend%C3%A9e&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Massacre_de_Machecoul.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1286" data-file-width="2126" height="121" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Massacre_de_Machecoul.jpg/200px-Massacre_de_Machecoul.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Massacre_de_Machecoul.jpg/300px-Massacre_de_Machecoul.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Massacre_de_Machecoul.jpg/400px-Massacre_de_Machecoul.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Massacre_de_Machecoul.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The massacre of 150 to 200 Vendean Republicans by Vendean Royalists in <a href="/wiki/Machecoul" title="Machecoul">Machecoul</a> was the starting event of the War in the Vendée.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Le_Vend%C3%A9en.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="413" data-file-width="252" height="361" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Le_Vend%C3%A9en.jpg/220px-Le_Vend%C3%A9en.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/14/Le_Vend%C3%A9en.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Le_Vend%C3%A9en.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Vendean rebel. Painting by <a href="/wiki/Julien_Le_Blant" title="Julien Le Blant">Julien Le Blant</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Class differences were not as great in the <a href="/wiki/Vend%C3%A9e" title="Vendée">Vendée</a> as in Paris or in other French provinces. In the rural Vendée, the local <a href="/wiki/Nobility" title="Nobility">nobility</a> seems to have been more permanently in residence and less bitterly resented than in other parts of France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alexis_de_Tocqueville" title="Alexis de Tocqueville">Alexis de Tocqueville</a> noted that most French nobles lived in cities by 1789. An Intendants' survey showed one of the few areas where they still lived with the peasants was the Vendée.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> Consequently, the conflicts that drove the revolution in Paris, for example, were also lessened in this particularly isolated part of France by the strong adherence of the population to their Catholic faith. In 1791, two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Representative_on_mission" title="Representative on mission">representatives on mission</a> informed the <a href="/wiki/National_Convention" title="National Convention">National Convention</a> of the disquieting condition of Vendée, and this news was quickly followed by the exposure of a royalist plot organized by the <a href="/wiki/Charles_Armand_Tuffin,_marquis_de_la_Rouerie" title="Charles Armand Tuffin, marquis de la Rouerie">Marquis de la Rouerie</a>. It was not until the social unrest and the fear of <a href="/wiki/Reign_of_Terror" title="Reign of Terror">The Terror</a> (a period between 1793–94 where tens of thousands of people were beheaded by use of guillotine) combined with the external pressures from the <a href="/wiki/Civil_Constitution_of_the_Clergy" title="Civil Constitution of the Clergy">Civil Constitution of the Clergy</a> (1790) and the introduction of a <a href="/wiki/Lev%C3%A9e_en_masse#The_French_Revolutionary_Wars" title="Levée en masse">levy</a> of 300,000 on the whole of France, decreed by the National Convention in February 1793, that the region erupted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anderson205_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Anderson205-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Furet124_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Furet124-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Civil Constitution of the Clergy required all clerics to swear allegiance to it and, by extension, to the increasingly anti-clerical <a href="/wiki/National_Constituent_Assembly" title="National Constituent Assembly">National Constituent Assembly</a>. All but seven of the 160 bishops refused the oath, as did about half of the parish priests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Joes-51_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Joes-51-10">[10]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Anti-clericalism" title="Anti-clericalism">Persecution of the clergy</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dechristianisation_of_France_during_the_French_Revolution" title="Dechristianisation of France during the French Revolution">of the faithful</a> was the first trigger of the rebellion; the second being conscription. Nonjuring priests were exiled or imprisoned and women on their way to Mass were beaten in the streets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Joes-51_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-Joes-51-10">[10]</a></sup> Religious orders were suppressed and Church property confiscated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Joes-51_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-Joes-51-10">[10]</a></sup> On 3 March 1793, virtually all the churches were ordered closed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Joes52_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Joes52-11">[11]</a></sup> Soldiers confiscated sacramental vessels and the people were forbidden to place crosses on graves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Joes52_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-Joes52-11">[11]</a></sup> Nearly all the purchasers of church land were <a href="/wiki/Bourgeoisie" title="Bourgeoisie">bourgeois</a>; very few peasants benefited from the sales.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>The March 1793 conscription requiring Vendeans to fill their district's quota of the national total of 300,000 enraged the populace,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anderson205_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-Anderson205-8">[8]</a></sup> who took up arms instead as "<a href="/wiki/Catholic_and_Royal_Army" title="Catholic and Royal Army">The Catholic Army</a>", "Royal" being added later, and fought for "above all the reopening of their parish churches with their former priests."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Joes-52-53_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Joes-52-53-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although town dwellers were more likely to support the Revolution in the Vendée,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> support for the revolution among the rural peasantry was not unknown. Many lived on monastery properties, and they overwhelmingly embraced the Revolution after these lands were seized and redistributed among them by the republican government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Outbreak_of_revolt">Outbreak of revolt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_the_Vend%C3%A9e&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Outbreak of revolt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coeur-chouan.jpeg"><img alt="A red cross supported by a heart" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="315" data-file-width="250" height="252" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Coeur-chouan.jpeg/200px-Coeur-chouan.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/51/Coeur-chouan.jpeg 1.5x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Coeur-chouan.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Sacred_Heart" title="Sacred Heart">Sacred Heart</a> patch of the Vendean royalist insurgents. The French motto 'Dieu, le Roi' means 'God, the King'.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There were other levy riots across France when regions started to draft men into the army in response to the Levy Decree in February. The reaction in the northwest in early March was particularly pronounced with large-scale rioting verging on insurrection. By early April, in areas north of the Loire, order had been restored by the revolutionary government, but south of the Loire in four departments that became known as the <i>Vendée militaire</i> there were few troops to control rebels and what had started as rioting quickly took on the form of a full insurrection led by priests and the local nobility.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>Within a few weeks the rebel forces had formed a substantial, if ill-equipped, army, the <i>Royal and Catholic Army</i>, supported by two thousand <a href="/wiki/Irregular_military" title="Irregular military">irregular</a> <a href="/wiki/Cavalry" title="Cavalry">cavalry</a> and a few captured <a href="/wiki/Artillery" title="Artillery">artillery</a> pieces. The main force of the rebels operated on a much smaller scale, using <a href="/wiki/Guerrilla_warfare" title="Guerrilla warfare">guerrilla tactics</a>, supported by the insurgents' unparalleled local knowledge and the good-will of the people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geographic_coverage">Geographic coverage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_the_Vend%C3%A9e&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Geographic coverage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vendee-militaire.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="739" data-file-width="1000" height="222" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Vendee-militaire.png/300px-Vendee-militaire.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Vendee-militaire.png/450px-Vendee-militaire.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Vendee-militaire.png/600px-Vendee-militaire.png 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vendee-militaire.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The administrative <a href="/wiki/Vend%C3%A9e" title="Vendée">Vendée</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/D%C3%A9partement" title="Département">département</a> (green), the "Military Vendée" (pink) where most of the insurrection took place and the <a href="/wiki/Vir%C3%A9e_de_Galerne" title="Virée de Galerne">Virée de Galerne</a> (black, red and blue arrows)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Geographically, the insurrection occurred within a rough <a href="/wiki/Quadrilateral" title="Quadrilateral">quadrilateral</a> approximately 60 miles (97 km) wide, with Cholet at its center. The territory defied description in the terms of the redistricting of 1790, nor did it align itself to descriptors used in the <i>Ancien Régime</i>; the heart of the movement lay in the forests, with Cholet at its center, in the wild districts of the old county of <a href="/wiki/Anjou" title="Anjou">Anjou</a>, in the Breton marshlands between Montaigu and the sea. It included parts of the old <a href="/wiki/Poitiers" title="Poitiers">Poitiers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tours" title="Tours">Tours</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Departement" title="Departement">departements</a> of <a href="/wiki/Maine-et-Loire" title="Maine-et-Loire">Maine-et-Loire</a>, the Vendée, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deux_S%C3%A8vres" title="Deux Sèvres">Deux Sèvres</a>, but never completely fell under insurgent control.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Vend.C3.A9e_military_response">Vendée military response</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_the_Vend%C3%A9e&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Vendée military response">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The revolt began in earnest in March 1793, as a rejection of the mass conscription. In February, the Convention had voted to approve a levy of three hundred thousand men, to be chosen by lot among the unmarried men in each commune. Thus, the arrival of recruiters reminded locals of the methods of the monarchy, aroused resistance nearly everywhere in the countryside, and set in motion the first serious signs of sedition. For the most part, much of this resistance was quelled quickly, but in the lower <a href="/wiki/Loire" title="Loire">Loire</a>, in the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mauges&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mauges (page does not exist)">Mauges</a> and in the Vendean <a href="/wiki/Bocage" title="Bocage">bocage</a>, the situation was more serious and more protracted. Youths from communes surrounding Cholet, a large textile town on the boundary between the two regions, invaded the town and killed the commander of the National Guard, a "patriotic" (pro-Revolutionary) manufacturer. Within a week, violence had spread to the Breton marshlands; peasants overran the town of <a href="/wiki/Machecoul" title="Machecoul">Machecoul</a> on 10–11 March, and several hundred "patriots" were <a href="/wiki/First_Massacre_of_Machecoul" title="First Massacre of Machecoul">massacred</a>. A large band of peasants under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Cathelineau" title="Jacques Cathelineau">Jacques Cathelineau</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jean-Nicolas_Stofflet" title="Jean-Nicolas Stofflet">Jean-Nicolas Stofflet</a> seized <a href="/wiki/Saint-Florent-le-Vieil" title="Saint-Florent-le-Vieil">Saint-Florent-le-Vieil</a>. On 19 March, a band of peasants attacked and scattered a small republican army of about 3,000 men on its way from <a href="/wiki/La_Rochelle" title="La Rochelle">La Rochelle</a> to <a href="/wiki/Nantes" title="Nantes">Nantes</a>. By mid-March, a minor revolt against conscription, had turned into an insurrection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FuretOzouf166_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-FuretOzouf166-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Republic was quick to respond, dispatching over 45,000 troops to the area. The first pitched battle was on the night of 19 March. A Republican column of 2,000, under <a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_Henri_Fran%C3%A7ois_de_Marc%C3%A9" title="fr:Louis Henri François de Marcé">Louis Henri François de Marcé</a>, moving from <a href="/wiki/La_Rochelle" title="La Rochelle">La Rochelle</a> to <a href="/wiki/Nantes" title="Nantes">Nantes</a>, was intercepted north of <a href="/wiki/Chantonnay" title="Chantonnay">Chantonnay</a> at Charrault bridge (<a href="/wiki/La_Gu%C3%A9rini%C3%A8re" title="La Guérinière">La Guérinière</a>), near the <a href="/wiki/Layon" title="Layon">Layon</a>. After six hours of fighting rebel reinforcements arrived and routed the Republican forces. In the north, on 22 March, another Republican force was routed near <a href="/wiki/Chalonnes-sur-Loire" title="Chalonnes-sur-Loire">Chalonnes-sur-Loire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>There followed a series of skirmishes and armed contacts:</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Battle_of_Bressuire">Battle of Bressuire</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_the_Vend%C3%A9e&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Battle of Bressuire">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 3 May 1793 Bressuire fell to Vendéen forces led by <a href="/wiki/Henri_de_la_Rochejaquelein" title="Henri de la Rochejaquelein">La Rochejacquelein</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Battle_of_Thouars">Battle of Thouars</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_the_Vend%C3%A9e&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Battle of Thouars">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bataille_de_Thouars_1793.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1391" data-file-width="1940" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Bataille_de_Thouars_1793.JPG/220px-Bataille_de_Thouars_1793.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Bataille_de_Thouars_1793.JPG/330px-Bataille_de_Thouars_1793.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Bataille_de_Thouars_1793.JPG/440px-Bataille_de_Thouars_1793.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bataille_de_Thouars_1793.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
La Rochejaquelein and the Marquis de Lescure leading troops on the pont de Vrine</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 5 May 1793. The main clash took place on the <i>Pont de Vrine</i>, the bridge over the <a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vrin_(rivi%C3%A8re)" title="fr:Vrin (rivière)">stream</a> leading into <a href="/wiki/Thouars" title="Thouars">Thouars</a>. The Vendéens proved unable to take the bridge for six hours, until <a href="/wiki/Louis_Marie_de_Lescure" title="Louis Marie de Lescure">Louis Marie de Lescure</a> (fighting in his first battle) showed himself alone on the bridge under enemy fire and encouraged his men to follow him, which they did, crossing the bridge. The Republicans there were taken from behind by the cavalry under <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Bonchamps" title="Charles de Bonchamps">Charles de Bonchamps</a>, which had crossed the river at a ford. Despite the arrival of reinforcements, the Republicans were routed and withdrew towards the city. The insurgents, headed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Henri_de_La_Rochejacquelein" title="Henri de La Rochejacquelein">Henri de La Rochejacquelein</a>, took the rampart by force and poured into the city, and the Republican troops quickly capitulated. The Vendéens seized a large amount of arms and gunpowder, but allowed the captured Republican forces to leave, after having sworn to no longer fight in the Vendée and had their hair shaved off so they could be recognised lest they went back on their word and were recaptured.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Battle_of_Fontenay-le-Comte">Battle of Fontenay-le-Comte</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_the_Vend%C3%A9e&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Battle of Fontenay-le-Comte">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 25 May 1793 the Catholic and royalist army took <a href="/wiki/Fontenay-le-Comte" title="Fontenay-le-Comte">Fontenay-le-Comte</a>. Lescure led his men in a courageous charge under enemy fire, shouting 'Long live the king!' and braving cannonfire, which left him unharmed. Likewise La Rochejacquelein wore his distinctive three red handkerchiefs on his head, waist and neck even though the gunners in the Republican forces were aiming for them. Following the victory his friends decided to copy him and all decided to wear three red handkerchiefs too so that La Rochejacquelein could not be distinguished by the enemy in the future. After this the only Vendée towns remaining in the control of the Republic were Nantes and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Les_Sables_d%27Olonne" title="Les Sables d'Olonne">Les Sables d'Olonne</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Battle_of_Saumur">Battle of Saumur</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_the_Vend%C3%A9e&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Battle of Saumur">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 9 June 1793, Vendean insurgents commanded by <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Cathelineau" title="Jacques Cathelineau">Jacques Cathelineau</a> captured the town of <a href="/wiki/Saumur" title="Saumur">Saumur</a> from <a href="/wiki/Louis-Alexandre_Berthier" title="Louis-Alexandre Berthier">Louis-Alexandre Berthier</a>. The victory gave the insurgents a massive supply of arms, including 50 cannon. This was the high point of the insurgency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> The Vendeans had never before attempted to take such a large town, and they captured it in a single day, inflicting heavy losses on its Republican defenders. Many prisoners were taken, some of whom went over to the Vendean cause, while many of the citizens fled to Tours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Incendie_Granville_1793.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1134" data-file-width="1752" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Incendie_Granville_1793.JPG/220px-Incendie_Granville_1793.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Incendie_Granville_1793.JPG/330px-Incendie_Granville_1793.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Incendie_Granville_1793.JPG/440px-Incendie_Granville_1793.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Incendie_Granville_1793.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The burning of <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Granville" title="Battle of Granville">Granville</a>, 14 November 1793</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Battle_of_Nantes">Battle of Nantes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_the_Vend%C3%A9e&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Battle of Nantes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 24 June 1793, the commanders of the Catholic and royalist army issued an ultimatum to the mayor of Nantes, <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9-Gaston_Baco_de_la_Chapelle" title="René-Gaston Baco de la Chapelle">Baco de la Chapelle</a> to surrender the city or they would massacre the garrison.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> On 29 June they began an assault with forces of 40,000. Inside the city were Republicans from the surrounding countryside who had fled to Nantes for safety, and fortified the defenders with tales of the horrors the rebels inflicted on towns they managed to take. Baco de la Chapelle stood on a dustcart which he called the 'chariot of victory' to urge the people on, even after he had been wounded in the leg. Poor coordination between the four Vendean armies led by <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_de_Charette" title="François de Charette">Charette</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Bonchamps" title="Charles de Bonchamps">Bonchamps</a>, Cathelineau and Lyrot hampered the assault, and Cathelineau's forces were delayed in their deployment by fighting along the <a href="/wiki/Erdre" title="Erdre">Erdre</a> river with a Republican battalion. Cathelineau himself was shot at the head of his forces, causing his men to lose heart and retreat, and ultimately the Vendeans were unable to take the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Battle_of_Ch.C3.A2tillon-sur-S.C3.A8vre">Battle of Châtillon-sur-Sèvre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_the_Vend%C3%A9e&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Battle of Châtillon-sur-Sèvre">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In July 1793, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jean_Baptiste_Kl%C3%A9ber" title="Jean Baptiste Kléber">Jean Baptiste Kléber</a> arrived from <a href="/wiki/Mainz" title="Mainz">Mainz</a> with a veteran army to suppress the rising. At the <a href="/wiki/First_Battle_of_Ch%C3%A2tillon" title="First Battle of Châtillon">First Battle of Châtillon</a>, southeast of <a href="/wiki/Cholet" title="Cholet">Cholet</a>, he inflicted one of the first defeats on the insurgents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Capture_Charette.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="494" data-file-width="647" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Capture_Charette.jpg/220px-Capture_Charette.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Capture_Charette.jpg/330px-Capture_Charette.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Capture_Charette.jpg/440px-Capture_Charette.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Capture_Charette.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The capture of <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_de_Charette" title="François de Charette">François de Charette</a>, 1796</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Battle_of_Vihiers">Battle of Vihiers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_the_Vend%C3%A9e&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Battle of Vihiers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Vendeans won a victory over the revolutionary army led by <a href="/wiki/Antoine_Joseph_Santerre" title="Antoine Joseph Santerre">Santerre</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Vihiers" title="Battle of Vihiers">Battle of Vihiers</a> on 18 July 1793.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Battle_of_Lu.C3.A7on">Battle of Luçon</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_the_Vend%C3%A9e&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Battle of Luçon">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lu%C3%A7on" title="Battle of Luçon">Battle of Luçon</a> was actually a series of three engagements fought over four weeks, the first on 15 July and the last on 14 August 1793, between Republican forces under <a href="/wiki/Augustin_Tuncq" title="Augustin Tuncq">Augustin Tuncq</a> and Vendean forces. The engagement on 14 August, fought near the town of <a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%A7on" title="Luçon">Luçon</a> was actually the conclusion of three engagements between <a href="/wiki/Louis_d%27Elb%C3%A9e" title="Louis d'Elbée">Louis d'Elbée</a>'s Vendean insurgents and the Republican army. On 15 July, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Claude_Sandoz&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Claude Sandoz (page does not exist)">Claude Sandoz</a> and a garrison of 800 had repulsed 5,000 insurgents led by d'Elbee; on 28 July, Tuncq drove off a second attempt; two weeks later, Tuncq and his 5,000 men routed 30,000 insurgents under the personal command of <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_de_Charette" title="François de Charette">François de Charette</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Battle_of_Montaigu">Battle of Montaigu</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_the_Vend%C3%A9e&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Battle of Montaigu">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Montaigu" title="Battle of Montaigu">Battle of Montaigu</a> was fought on 21 September 1793 when the Vendéens attacked general Jean-Michel Beysser's French Republican division. Taken by surprise, this division fought back but lost 400 men, including many captured. Some of these prisoners were summarily executed by the Vendeens and their bodies later found in the castle wells by troops under Jean-Baptiste Kléber.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_Battle_of_Tiffauges">Second Battle of Tiffauges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_the_Vend%C3%A9e&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Second Battle of Tiffauges">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Tiffauges" title="Battle of Tiffauges">Battle of Tiffauges</a> was fought on 19 September 1793 between Royalist military leaders against Republican troops under Jean-Baptiste Kléber and Canclaux.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_Battle_of_Chatillon">Second Battle of Chatillon</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_the_Vend%C3%A9e&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Second Battle of Chatillon">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Second_Battle_of_Ch%C3%A2tillon" title="Second Battle of Châtillon">Second Battle of Châtillon</a> was fought on 11 October 1793</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Battle_of_Tremblaye">Battle of Tremblaye</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_the_Vend%C3%A9e&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Battle of Tremblaye">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_La_Tremblaye" title="Battle of La Tremblaye">Battle of Tremblaye</a> (15 October 1793) took place near Cholet during the war in the Vendée, and was a Republican victory over the Vendéens. The Vendean leader Lescure was seriously injured in the fighting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Defeat">Defeat</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_the_Vend%C3%A9e&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Defeat">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fusillades_de_Nantes.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="884" data-file-width="1924" height="115" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Fusillades_de_Nantes.jpg/250px-Fusillades_de_Nantes.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Fusillades_de_Nantes.jpg/375px-Fusillades_de_Nantes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Fusillades_de_Nantes.jpg/500px-Fusillades_de_Nantes.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fusillades_de_Nantes.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mass shootings at Nantes, 1793</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 1 August 1793, the <a href="/wiki/Committee_of_Public_Safety" title="Committee of Public Safety">Committee of Public Safety</a> ordered General <a href="/wiki/Jean-Baptiste_Carrier" title="Jean-Baptiste Carrier">Jean-Baptiste Carrier</a> to carry out a "pacification" of the region by complete physical destruction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-31">[31]</a></sup> These orders were not carried out immediately, but a steady stream of demands for total destruction persisted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-31">[31]</a></sup> Under orders from the Committee of Public Safety in February 1794, the Republican forces launched their final "pacification" effort (named <i>Vendée-Vengé</i> or "Vendée Avenged"): twelve columns, the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colonnes_infernales" title="Colonnes infernales">colonnes infernales</a></i> ("infernal columns") under <a href="/wiki/Louis_Marie_Turreau" title="Louis Marie Turreau">Louis Marie Turreau</a>, marched through the Vendée.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> General Turreau inquired about "the fate of the women and children I will encounter in rebel territory", stating that, if it was "necessary to pass them all by sword", he would require a decree.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_31-2"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-31">[31]</a></sup> In response, the Committee of Public Safety ordered him to "eliminate the brigands to the last man, there is your duty..."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_31-3"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Republican army was reinforced, benefiting from the first men of the <i><a href="/wiki/Lev%C3%A9e_en_masse" title="Levée en masse">levée en masse</a></i> and reinforcements from <a href="/wiki/Mainz" title="Mainz">Mainz</a>. The Vendean army had its first serious defeat at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cholet" title="Battle of Cholet">Battle of Cholet</a> on 17 October; worse for the rebels, their army was split. In October 1793 the main force, commanded by <a href="/wiki/Henri_de_la_Rochejaquelein" title="Henri de la Rochejaquelein">Henri de la Rochejaquelein</a> and numbering some 25,000 (followed by thousands of civilians of all ages), crossed the Loire, headed for the port of <a href="/wiki/Granville,_Manche" title="Granville, Manche">Granville</a> where they expected to be greeted by a British fleet and an army of exiled French nobles. Arriving at Granville, they found the city surrounded by Republican forces, with no British ships in sight. Their attempts to take the city were unsuccessful. During the retreat, the extended columns fell prey to Republican forces; suffering from hunger and disease, they died in the thousands. The force was defeated in the last, decisive <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Savenay" title="Battle of Savenay">Battle of Savenay</a> on 23 December.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Taylor1913_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-Taylor1913-33">[33]</a></sup> Among those executed the following day was lieutenant-general <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Alexis_de_Verteuil" title="Jacques Alexis de Verteuil">Jacques Alexis de Verteuil</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Travers%C3%A9e_de_la_Loire_Vend%C3%A9e.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="750" data-file-width="1278" height="129" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Travers%C3%A9e_de_la_Loire_Vend%C3%A9e.jpg/220px-Travers%C3%A9e_de_la_Loire_Vend%C3%A9e.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Travers%C3%A9e_de_la_Loire_Vend%C3%A9e.jpg/330px-Travers%C3%A9e_de_la_Loire_Vend%C3%A9e.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Travers%C3%A9e_de_la_Loire_Vend%C3%A9e.jpg/440px-Travers%C3%A9e_de_la_Loire_Vend%C3%A9e.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Travers%C3%A9e_de_la_Loire_Vend%C3%A9e.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Crossing the Loire: General Lescure, wounded, crosses the Loire at Saint-Florent, by Jules Girardet</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>With this came formal orders for forced evacuation; also, a '<a href="/wiki/Scorched_earth" title="Scorched earth">scorched earth</a>' policy was initiated: farms were destroyed, crops and forests burned and villages razed. There were many reported atrocities and a campaign of mass killing universally targeted at residents of the Vendée regardless of combatant status, political affiliation, age or gender.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>From January to May 1794, 20,000 to 50,000 Vendean civilians were massacred by the <a href="/wiki/Infernal_columns" title="Infernal columns">Infernal columns</a> of the general <a href="/wiki/Louis_Marie_Turreau" title="Louis Marie Turreau">Louis Marie Turreau</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Anjou" title="Anjou">Anjou</a>, directed by <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Hentz" title="Nicolas Hentz">Nicolas Hentz</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Marie_Pierre_Adrien_Francastel&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Marie Pierre Adrien Francastel (page does not exist)">Marie Pierre Adrien Francastel</a>, Republicans captured 11,000 to 15,000 Vendeans, 6,500 to 7,000 were shot or guillotined and 2,000 to 2,200 prisoners died from disease.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ex%C3%A9cution_Charette.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1809" data-file-width="2388" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Ex%C3%A9cution_Charette.jpg/300px-Ex%C3%A9cution_Charette.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Ex%C3%A9cution_Charette.jpg/450px-Ex%C3%A9cution_Charette.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Ex%C3%A9cution_Charette.jpg/600px-Ex%C3%A9cution_Charette.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ex%C3%A9cution_Charette.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Execution of General Charette, in Nantes, March 1796, by <a href="/wiki/Julien_Le_Blant" title="Julien Le Blant">Julien Le Blant</a>, c. 1883</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>General Westermann reported to his political masters at the Convention: "The Vendée is no more ... According to your orders, I have trampled their children beneath our horses' feet; I have massacred their women, so they will no longer give birth to brigands. I do not have a single prisoner to reproach me. I have exterminated them all."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Some historians believe this letter never existed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> The rebellion was still going on, and there were several thousand living Vendéan prisoners being held by Westerman's forces when the letter was supposedly written.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> The killing of civilians would also have been an explicit violation of the Convention's orders to Westermann.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Convention issued conciliatory proclamations allowing the Vendeans liberty of worship and guaranteeing their property. <a href="/wiki/Lazare_Hoche" title="Lazare Hoche">General Hoche</a> applied these measures with great success. He restored their cattle to the peasants who submitted, "let the priests have a few crowns", and on 20 July 1795 annihilated an <i>émigré</i> expedition which had been equipped in England and had seized Fort Penthièvre and <a href="/wiki/Quiberon" title="Quiberon">Quiberon</a>. Treaties were concluded at <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=La_Jaunaie&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="La Jaunaie (page does not exist)">La Jaunaie</a> (15 February 1795) and at <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=La_Mabillaie&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="La Mabillaie (page does not exist)">La Mabillaie</a>, and were fairly well observed by the Vendeans; no obstacle remained but the feeble and scattered remnant of the Vendeans still under arms and the <a href="/wiki/Chouannerie" title="Chouannerie">Chouans</a>. On 30 July 1796 the state of siege was raised in the western departments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EBEE-Wars_Of_The_Vendee_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-EBEE-Wars_Of_The_Vendee-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>Estimates of those killed in the Vendean conflict – on both sides – range between 117,000 and 450,000, out of a population of around 800,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mcphee_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-mcphee-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_revolts">Later revolts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_the_Vend%C3%A9e&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Later revolts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>According to Theodore A. Dodge,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> the war in Vendée lasted with intensity from 1793 to 1799, when it was suppressed, but later broke out spasmodically especially in 1813, 1814 and 1815. During <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Hundred_Days" title="Hundred Days">Hundred Days</a> in 1815, some of the population of Vendée remained loyal to King <a href="/wiki/Louis_XVIII_of_France" title="Louis XVIII of France">Louis XVIII</a>, forcing Napoleon – who was short of troops to fight the Waterloo Campaign – to send a force of 10,000 under the command of <a href="/wiki/Jean_Maximilien_Lamarque" title="Jean Maximilien Lamarque">Jean Maximilien Lamarque</a> to pacify the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB1911WC_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-EB1911WC-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Genocide_controversy">Genocide controversy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_the_Vend%C3%A9e&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Genocide controversy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chouans_in_the_Vendee.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="462" data-file-width="789" height="117" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Chouans_in_the_Vendee.png/200px-Chouans_in_the_Vendee.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Chouans_in_the_Vendee.png/300px-Chouans_in_the_Vendee.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Chouans_in_the_Vendee.png/400px-Chouans_in_the_Vendee.png 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chouans_in_the_Vendee.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Soldiers, women, and children embroiled in a fight near a church</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The popular <a href="/wiki/Historiography" title="Historiography">historiography</a> of the War in the Vendée is deeply rooted in conflicts between different schools of French historiography, and, as a result, writings on the uprising are generally highly partisan, coming down strongly in support of the revolutionary government or the Vendéen royalists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> This conflict originated in the 19th century between two groups of historians, the <i>Bleus</i>, named for their support of the republicans, who based their findings on archives from the uprising and the <i>Blancs</i>, named for their support of the monarchy and the Catholic Church, who based their findings on local oral histories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jean-Cl.C3.A9ment_Martin_2007.2C_pp._70_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jean-Cl.C3.A9ment_Martin_2007.2C_pp._70-50">[50]</a></sup> The <i>Bleus</i> generally argued that the Vendée was not a popular uprising, but was the result of noble and clerical manipulation of the peasantry. One of the leaders of this school of thought, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Charles-Louis_Chassin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Charles-Louis Chassin (page does not exist)">Charles-Louis Chassin</a>, published eleven volumes of letters, archives, and other materials supporting this position. The <i>Blancs</i>, generally members of the former nobility and clergy themselves, argued (frequently using the same documents as Chassin, but also drawing from contemporary memoirs and oral histories) that the peasants were acting out of a genuine love for the nobility and a desire to protect the Catholic Church.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jean-Cl.C3.A9ment_Martin_2007.2C_pp._70_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jean-Cl.C3.A9ment_Martin_2007.2C_pp._70-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>This focus was popularized in the English-speaking world in 1986, with French historian Reynald Secher's <i>A French Genocide: The Vendée</i>. Secher argued that the actions of the French republican government during the War in the Vendée was the first modern <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SR-Vend.C3.A9e_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-SR-Vend.C3.A9e-51">[51]</a></sup> Secher's claims caused a minor uproar in France amongst scholars of modern French history, as many mainstream authorities on the period – both French and foreign – published articles rejecting Secher's claims.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Claude Langlois (of the Institute of History of the French Revolution) derides Secher's claims as "quasi-mythological".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CL-426.E2.80.93434_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-CL-426.E2.80.93434-57">[57]</a></sup> Timothy Tackett of the University of California summarizes the case as such: "In reality ... the Vendée was a tragic civil war with endless horrors committed by both sides – initiated, in fact, by the rebels themselves. The Vendeans were no more blameless than were the republicans. The use of the word genocide is wholly inaccurate and inappropriate."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Hugh Gough (Professor of history at <a href="/wiki/University_College_Dublin" title="University College Dublin">University College Dublin</a>) called Secher's book an attempt at <a href="/wiki/Historical_revisionism" title="Historical revisionism">historical revisionism</a> unlikely to have any lasting impact.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup>While some such as Peter McPhee roundly criticized Secher, including the assertion of commonality between the functions of the Republican government and Communist totalitarianism. Historian <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Chaunu" title="Pierre Chaunu">Pierre Chaunu</a> expressed support for Secher's views,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-google105_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-google105-60">[60]</a></sup> describing the events as the first "ideological genocide".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FUSILLADES.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="163" data-file-width="244" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/FUSILLADES.jpg/210px-FUSILLADES.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b0/FUSILLADES.jpg 1.5x" width="210"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FUSILLADES.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Shootings and massacres by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colonnes_infernales" title="Colonnes infernales">Colonnes infernales</a> under Turreau</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Critics of Secher's thesis have alleged that his methodology is flawed. McPhee asserted that these errors are as follows: (1) The war was not fought against Vendeans but Royalist Vendeans, the government relied on the support of Republican Vendeans; (2) the Convention ended the campaign after the Royalist Army was clearly defeated – if the aim was genocide, then they would have continued and easily exterminated the population; (3) Fails to inform the reader of atrocities committed by Royalist against Republicans in the Vendée; (4) Repeats stories now known to be folkloric myths as fact; (5) Does not refer to the wide range of estimates of deaths suffered by both sides, and that casualties were not "one-sided"; and more.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mcphee_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-mcphee-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Noyades_de_Nantes-Joseph_Aubert.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="540" data-file-width="1280" height="105" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Noyades_de_Nantes-Joseph_Aubert.gif/250px-Noyades_de_Nantes-Joseph_Aubert.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Noyades_de_Nantes-Joseph_Aubert.gif/375px-Noyades_de_Nantes-Joseph_Aubert.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Noyades_de_Nantes-Joseph_Aubert.gif/500px-Noyades_de_Nantes-Joseph_Aubert.gif 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Noyades_de_Nantes-Joseph_Aubert.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Drownings_at_Nantes" title="Drownings at Nantes">Drownings at Nantes</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Peter McPhee says that the pacification of the Vendée does not fit either the United Nations' <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CPPCG" title="CPPCG">CPPCG</a> definition of genocide because the events happened during a civil war. He states that the war in the Vendée was not a one-sided mass killing and the Committee of Public Safety did not intend to exterminate the whole population of the Vendée; parts of the population were allied to the revolutionary government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mcphee_46-2"><a href="#cite_note-mcphee-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>Concerning the controversy, Michel Vovelle, a specialist on the French Revolution, remarked: "A whole literature is forming on "Franco-French genocide", starting from risky estimates of the number of fatalities in the Vendean wars ... Despite not being specialists in the subject, historians such as Pierre Chaunu have put all the weight of their great moral authority behind the development of an anathematizing discourse, and have dismissed any effort to look at the subject reasonably."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>Debate over the characterization of the Vendée uprising was renewed in 2007, when nine deputies introduced a measure to the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_(France)" title="National Assembly (France)"><i>Assemblée nationale</i></a> to officially recognize the republican actions as genocidal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> The measure was strongly denounced by a group of leftist French historians as an attempt to use history to justify political extremism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Challenging_the_methodology">Challenging the methodology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_the_Vend%C3%A9e&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Challenging the methodology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the heart of the modern controversy lies Secher's evidence, which <a href="/wiki/Charles_Tilly" title="Charles Tilly">Charles Tilly</a> analyzed in 1990.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> Initially, Tilly maintains, Secher completed a thoughtful <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dissertation" title="Dissertation">dissertation</a>-style thesis about the revolutionary experience in his own village, <a href="/wiki/La_Chapelle-Basse-Mer" title="La Chapelle-Basse-Mer">La Chapelle-Basse-Mer</a>, which lies near Nantes. In the published version of his thesis, he incorporated some of Tilly's own arguments: that conflicts within communities generalized into a region-wide confrontation of anti-revolutionary majority based in the countryside with a pro-revolutionary minority that had particular strength in the cities. The split formed with the application of the Civil Constitution of the Clergy and the oath to support it, in 1790–1792. From then, the local conflicts grew more sharply defined, over the choice between juring and non-juring priests. The conscription of March 1793, with the questionable exemption for Republican officials and National Guard members, broadened the anti-revolutionary coalition and brought the young men into action.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>With <i>Le génocide français</i>, Reynald Secher's thesis for the <i>Doctorat d'État</i> began with a generalization of the standard arguments to the whole region. Although La Chapelle-Basse-Mer served him repeatedly as a reference point, Secher illustrated his arguments with wide citations from national and regional archives to establish a broader frame of reference. Furthermore, he drew on graphic, nineteenth century accounts widely known to the historians of the Vendee: Carrier drownings and the "infernal columns of Turreau". Most importantly, however, Secher broke with conventional assessments by asserting on the basis of minimal evidence, Tilly claims, that the pre-revolutionary Vendée was more prosperous than the rest of France (to better emphasize the devastation of the war and the repression). He used dubious statistical methods to establish population losses and fatalities, statistical processes that inflated the number of people in the region, the number and value of houses, and the financial losses of the region. Secher's statistical procedure relied on three unjustifiable assumptions. First, Secher assumes a constant birth rate of about 37 per thousand of population, when actually, Tilly maintains, the population was declining. Second, Secher assumes no net migration; Tilly maintains that thousands fled the region, or at least shifted where they lived within the region. Finally, Secher understated the population present at the end of the conflict by ending it 1802, not 1794.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>Despite the criticism, a number of scholars continue the assertion of genocide. In addition to Secher and Chaunu, Kurt Jonassohn and Frank Chalk also consider it a case of genocide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Further support comes from <a href="/wiki/Adam_Jones_(Canadian_scholar)" title="Adam Jones (Canadian scholar)">Adam Jones</a>, who wrote in <i>Genocide: A Comprehensive Introduction</i> a summary of the Vendée uprising, supporting the view that it was a genocide: "the Vendée Uprising stands as a notable example of a mass killing campaign that has only recently been conceptualized as 'genocide'" and that while this designation "is not universally shared ... it seems apt in the light of the large scale murder of a designated group (the Vendéan civilian population)."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Chaunu" title="Pierre Chaunu">Pierre Chaunu</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-google105_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-google105-60">[60]</a></sup> describes it as the first "ideological genocide".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> Mark Levene, a historian who specializes in the study of genocide,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> considers the Vendée "an archetype of modern genocide".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Other scholars who consider the massacres to be genocide include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/R.J._Rummel" title="R.J. Rummel">R.J. Rummel</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jean_Tulard" title="Jean Tulard">Jean Tulard</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> and Anthony James Joes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Historiography">Historiography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_the_Vend%C3%A9e&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Historiography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>This relatively brief episode in French history has left significant traces on French politics, as the current argument on genocide suggests, yet it is reasonable to see the episode, Charles Tilly has claimed, in a far more benign light:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>West's counterrevolution grew directly from the efforts of revolutionary officials to install a particular kind of direct rule in the region: a rule that practically eliminated nobles and priests from their positions as partly autonomous intermediaries, that brought the state's demands for taxes, manpower, and deference to the level of individual communities, neighborhoods, and households that gave the region's bourgeois political power they had never before wielded. In seeking to extend the state's rule to every locality, and to dislodge all enemies of that rule, French revolutionaries started a process that did not cease for twenty-five years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>The Vendée revolt became an immediate symbol of confrontation between revolution and counterrevolution, and a source of unexpurgated violence. The region, and its towns, were eliminated; even the department name of <i>Vendée</i> was renamed <i>Venge</i>. Towns and cities were also renamed, but at heart, in villages and farms, the old names remained the same. Beyond the controversial interpretations of genocide, other historians posit the insurrection as a revolt against conscription that cascaded to include other complaints. For a period of several months, control of the Vendée slipped from the hands of Parisian revolutionaries. They ascribed the revolt to the resurgence of royalist ideas: when faced with insurrection of the people against the Revolution of the People, they were unable to see it as anything <i>but</i> an aristocratic plot. <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mona_Ozouf&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mona Ozouf (page does not exist)">Mona Ozouf</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Furet" title="François Furet">François Furet</a> maintain it was not. The entire territory, none of it unified under a single idea from the <i>ancien regime</i>, had never been a region morally at odds with the rest of the nation. It was not the fall of the old regime that aroused the population against the Revolution, but rather the construction of the new regime into locally unacceptable principles and forms: the new map of districts and departments, the administrative dictatorship, and above all the non-juring priests. Rebellion had first flared in August 1792, but had been immediately quelled. Even the <a href="/wiki/Execution_of_Louis_XVI" title="Execution of Louis XVI">regicide</a> did not trigger insurrection. What did was the forced conscription. Although the Vendeans, to use the term loosely, wrote God and King large on their flags, they invested those symbols of their tradition with something other than regret for the lost regime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Film">Film</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_the_Vend%C3%A9e&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Film">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The uprising in the Vendée was the subject of an independent feature film from Navis Pictures. <i>The War of the Vendée</i> (2012), written and directed by Jim Morlino, won awards for "Best Film For Young Audiences", (Mirabile Dictu International Catholic Film Festival – at the Vatican) and "Best Director" (John Paul II International Film Festival – Miami, FL). The Vendée Revolt was the setting for one of the BBC’s The Scarlet Pimpernel series entitled Valentin Gautier. (2002) The Vendée Revolt was also the setting for "<a href="/wiki/The_Frogs_and_the_Lobsters" title="The Frogs and the Lobsters">The Frogs and the Lobsters</a>", an episode of the television program <i><a href="/wiki/Hornblower_(TV_series)" title="Hornblower (TV series)">Hornblower</a></i>. It is set during the French revolutionary wars and very loosely based on the chapter of the same name in <a href="/wiki/C._S._Forester" title="C. S. Forester">C. S. Forester</a>'s novel, <i><a href="/wiki/Mr._Midshipman_Hornblower" title="Mr. Midshipman Hornblower">Mr. Midshipman Hornblower</a></i> and on the actual ill-fated <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_France_(1795)" title="Invasion of France (1795)">Quiberon expedition</a> of 1795.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_the_Vend%C3%A9e&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-hussenet-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-hussenet_1-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-hussenet_1-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-hussenet_1-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-hussenet_1-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Jacques Hussenet (dir.), <i>« Détruisez la Vendée ! » Regards croisés sur les victimes et destructions de la guerre de Vendée</i>, La Roche-sur-Yon, Centre vendéen de recherches historiques, 2007</span></li>
